<div id="review_975630118" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975630118" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1254714-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513279210p2/1254714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/975630118?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/1254714-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1254714-steve?shelf=sci-fi-and-fantasy">sci-fi-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer975630118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7883029160862634681">With a third of the book to go, I lost interest. The mystical (and often contradictory) mumbo-jumbo, the increasing sense that I was simply reading a recasting of Dune, the endless pregnant speeches that suggest more than they deliver, just drove me into the ground like a tent post. All of that said, I really enjoyed the first half of the book. Herbert's endless wheels-within-wheels plots, revenge, the weird cultures, etc., are pretty cool. However, by the end (among various outrages) I thought </span>
  <span id="freeText7883029160862634681" style="display:none">With a third of the book to go, I lost interest. The mystical (and often contradictory) mumbo-jumbo, the increasing sense that I was simply reading a recasting of Dune, the endless pregnant speeches that suggest more than they deliver, just drove me into the ground like a tent post. All of that said, I really enjoyed the first half of the book. Herbert's endless wheels-within-wheels plots, revenge, the weird cultures, etc., are pretty cool. However, by the end (among various outrages) I thought the chief crime was how the wonderfully strange character of Alia had been flattened out and misused. (The "return" of the Baron, after his deliciously Shakespearian demise, pissed me off.) No one ever seems to die forever in a Herbert book, and I think that's a problem. Re-booting characters probably should be a no-go zone in a multi book series. Well, at least the brutal George Martin understands the importance of (literally) killing your darlings. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7883029160862634681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2194836433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194836433" />
    <a title="Skylar Phelps" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41541918-skylar-phelps"><img alt="Skylar Phelps" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575827186p2/41541918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194836433?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skylar Phelps" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skylar Phelps" href="/user/show/41541918-skylar-phelps">Skylar Phelps</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194836433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15837337883490876146">This series as a whole is mind bending. It is a tough read, with lots of complexity, an unprecedented amount of world/universe building and a tedious new vocabulary but it’s well worth it. I just finished Children of Dune and my brain feels like it’s cooling down from a hefty workout. In a good and satisfying way. <br/><br/>If you read the series, stick with it and prepare to be amazed. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

I was absolutely engrossed from start to finish, and I could hardly put it down (as you can see from the "date started" and "date finished" numbers). I am excited to read book 4!</span>

<div id="review_3500914798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780593098240" href="/book/show/44492286-children-of-dune">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42490432-bart?shelf=speculative">speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42490432-bart?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3500914798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6389591474961073487"><b>“The landscape which met their gaze was beyond pity, nowhere did it pause – no hesitations in it at all.”</b><br/><br/>There is something relentless to Children of Dune. It was the most difficult hurdle yet in my project of rereading the entire series.<br/><br/>It is a bit of a surprise this became “the first hardcover best-seller ever in the science fiction field” and also won the 1977 Hugo, because there is undeniably truth in David Pringle’s assessment of the book being “convoluted stuff.”<br/><br/>There’s a paradox to this v</span>
  <span id="freeText6389591474961073487" style="display:none"><b>“The landscape which met their gaze was beyond pity, nowhere did it pause – no hesitations in it at all.”</b><br /><br />There is something relentless to Children of Dune. It was the most difficult hurdle yet in my project of rereading the entire series.<br /><br />It is a bit of a surprise this became “the first hardcover best-seller ever in the science fiction field” and also won the 1977 Hugo, because there is undeniably truth in David Pringle’s assessment of the book being “convoluted stuff.”<br /><br />There’s a paradox to this very review and how it determined my reading experience, and it has to do with that convolutedness. Because I knew I wanted to write this text, I read Children carefully – maybe too carefully, taking notes, trying to figure things out. Especially in the second half of the book, that left me gasping for air at times, unable to figure out what Herbert wanted to do, lost in the mystical ramblings about visions and futures, focusing on inconsistencies or what I thought were inconsistencies. It took a bit of joy out of reading.<br /><br />At the same time, I did like the overall plot a lot, and could see Herbert had actually managed to tell yet another great story with perfect pacing, especially when the action kicked in: his characteristic style of cutting between short scenes with lots of dialogue somehow delivered the goods again. All that left me with about a 3 out of 5 stars tally, a bit in line with when I first read the series, and I then thought book 2 and 3 were the weakest of the six.<br /><br />But when I started to reread (and reread and reread) all the quotes I had marked to get a better grip on the book’s difficult stuff, I actually understood more of it, and most inconsistencies dissolved. So yes, this review at times wrecked my reading – instead of just riding the flow, I focused too much on trying to understand – but in the end it also reconciled me with the book. That leaves me with a 3.5, maybe 4 star rating, because I still think Herbert could have cut back some on the mystic philosophy, without actually hurting its core.<br /><br />In what follows, I first tried to write something of a review of the book: strengths, weaknesses, characters, you know the drill. <b>I primarily focus on Alia as tragic figure, and also discuss an important thing that remains unclear &amp; possibly inconsistent: Paul’s relationship to the Golden Path.</b><br /><br />For those that want to dive in even deeper, <b>after that first part, I zoom in on four very specific subjects: how I think ‘change’ is the central concept of this book, the prevalence of a Nietzschean Amor Fati, the book’s relationship with Nietzsche’s morality beyond good &amp; evil, and finally, free will and its relation to Leto II’s specific version of prescience.</b><br /><br />Both parts are a spoiler bonanza, but I guess this kind of writing will not appeal to those who haven’t read the books anyway.<br /><br />The text is heavy with quotes, but I wrote it so that you can still follow the logic if you skip them – except once, and I’ll warn you there. The quotes are for the die-hards. I had 9504 words selected out of the book, of which I used about 6200. Add to that my own 4400 words, and abracadabra …another long read, totaling 10630 words. It is what it is, I couldn’t help it. A full, thorough discussion of the book needed those.<br /><br />(...)<br /><br /><a href="https://schicksalgemeinschaft.wordpress.com/2020/08/17/children-of-dune-frank-herbert-1976/" rel="nofollow noopener">Full analysis on Weighing A Pig Doesn't Fatten It</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6389591474961073487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_139661079" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139661079" />
    <a title="Michael Tildsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2717220-michael-tildsley"><img alt="Michael Tildsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442976905p2/2717220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139661079?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Tildsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Tildsley" href="/user/show/2717220-michael-tildsley">Michael Tildsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425074992" href="/book/show/1455421.Children_of_Dune">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139661079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8525136983691331586">This one is officially my favorite of the series. Herbert's narrative style has been honed and refined in this sequel. The result is a novel with a lot more showing and a lot less telling. The telling that remains now is there mostly to help the reader bridge the nine year gap between novels. <br/><br/>What can I say about the plot without giving anything away? It was far-reaching, character-filled, and cerebral. There is a short slump in the middle where I felt like Herbert could have cut this into two n</span>
  <span id="freeText8525136983691331586" style="display:none">This one is officially my favorite of the series. Herbert's narrative style has been honed and refined in this sequel. The result is a novel with a lot more showing and a lot less telling. The telling that remains now is there mostly to help the reader bridge the nine year gap between novels. <br /><br />What can I say about the plot without giving anything away? It was far-reaching, character-filled, and cerebral. There is a short slump in the middle where I felt like Herbert could have cut this into two novels, but this one is mostly a wild sandworm ride that kept me reading from cover to cover. The themes and overtones do not tread lightly, but I admire that and I didn't feel preached to, except when I was meant to feel preached to. <br /><br />I admit I didn't really buy the shift in Alia's character at first because I had not placed the context. Herbert does well to show us that grief and time can do scary things to a human soul. <br /><br />I have high hopes for the rest of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8525136983691331586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1122842692563522840">[placeholder]<br/><br/>Some bits were amazing, most parts I liked, very few meh parts. So being a mash of like/reallylike/meh/amazing makes it... a 3? 4? 4.5? I honestly do not want to give a rating here! The series so far though has been nothing short of fascinating - what I really enjoy is the underlying culture/philosophy/world-building! Hoho. So... I guess I should give a it 4? Not as epic as the first book, not as heart wrenching as the second book - but well worth the read (for me) - although that s</span>
  <span id="freeText1122842692563522840" style="display:none">[placeholder]<br /><br />Some bits were amazing, most parts I liked, very few meh parts. So being a mash of like/reallylike/meh/amazing makes it... a 3? 4? 4.5? I honestly do not want to give a rating here! The series so far though has been nothing short of fascinating - what I really enjoy is the underlying culture/philosophy/world-building! Hoho. So... I guess I should give a it 4? Not as epic as the first book, not as heart wrenching as the second book - but well worth the read (for me) - although that showdown at the end a tad bit overdramatic haha (I would like to see a live action of that scene though!). <br /><br />... I just checked my ebook reader and there are a tonne of annotations in there. If that doesn't tell you how much I enjoyed the book then I guess nothing will. Haha.<br /><br />I may write a review somewhere down the line or I may not. We'll see. I do plan to read on until at least Book Six at some point down the road. Wish me luck!<br /><br />Source: Google Play Store<br />First finished: 5jun2018</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cRkpA0sepZ3sQI9GOSE9HJLAvvLRQ/SpJ7fzCbIMvszAB+nZwB2yrd3dVSAgMlNVzPboeJQexIgv/VzsdsU2KA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i6rHPQGcoagMGGh2k+3W76ga2rTPcd6FMxaLLWlXUBc6tAfnip+2mD2FshCK/rim9iyMPoos7qQ7XCTIrZ7Y8w==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_7967').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_7967').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_7967').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11702332601083822960">Frank Herbert was a critically acclaimed and commercially successful American science fiction author.<br/><br/>He is best known for the novel <i>Dune</i> and its five sequels. The Dune saga, set in the distant future and taking place over millennia, dealt with themes such as human survival and evolution, ecology, and the intersection of religion, politics, and power, and is widely considered to be among the classi</span>
  <span id="freeText11702332601083822960" style="display:none">Frank Herbert was a critically acclaimed and commercially successful American science fiction author.<br /><br />He is best known for the novel <i>Dune</i> and its five sequels. The Dune saga, set in the distant future and taking place over millennia, dealt with themes such as human survival and evolution, ecology, and the intersection of religion, politics, and power, and is widely considered to be among the classics in the field of science fiction.<br /><br />He was the father of fellow author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/56.Brian_Herbert" title="Brian Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Brian Herbert</a>.</span>
